Wang Yansong Formulates 149

Practical Measures for Using Domestic Goods – To Be Implemented After Consultation with the Municipal Government – The 22nd meeting of the Shanghai Municipal Party Headquarters discussed the proposal to strictly prohibit party and government personnel from wearing Western-style clothing and should switch to wearing domestic goods to promote them. It was resolved that Committee Member Wang Yansong would be publicly recommended to consult with the Municipal Government on handling the matter. It is heard that Mr. Wang has formulated several practical measures and sent them to the Municipal Government for consideration in order to negotiate and implement them. The original text is recorded below:

Since promoting domestic goods is an urgent task, it must first start with party and government personnel in order to achieve the effect of setting an example and imitating from above. According to the original intention of the proposal from the Second Direct Branch, the following measures are drafted: (1) The Party Headquarters and the government shall each strictly order staff members to use domestic goods and set up a registration office to register foreign clothes made in the past within a time limit, and then affix certificates. However, these foreign clothes with certificates attached may still not be worn at formal gatherings to avoid misunderstanding among the public. (2) Party and government personnel who violate the above order shall be severely punished, and the standard of punishment shall be based on dereliction of duty. (3) The Party and government should jointly announce to all the people's organizations in the city that all staff members should use domestic goods, and the Party Headquarters should send people to inspect them at any time. Those who cannot comply will be given a warning, or their positions will be suspended in severe cases. (4) When the Party and government and various agencies and organizations hold Dr. Sun Yat-sen Memorial Week every week, the person in charge must check whether the people in the meeting are actually using domestic goods and constantly admonish them. (5) The best way to punish party and government officials for wearing foreign goods is to set up a drafting committee to draft special rules for approval and implementation. (6) The above measures must be strictly implemented. The above are only some temporary opinions, and I still ask your government to consider them in order to negotiate and implement them. Please accept my sentiments. Shanghaimunicipal government

Beginning Today 152

Hong Kong Also Bans Silver Imports - Why the Rush of Huge Amounts of Shanghai Silver? - Two Million in Silver Transported to India - After the promulgation of the Shanghai silver ban, foreign silver imported into Shanghai could no longer be unloaded in Shanghai and was mostly transferred to Hong Kong. Recently, the Hong Kong authorities issued an order banning the import of Mexican silver dollars. However, Yuan head coins could still be transported there. Yesterday, banks and shipping companies in Shanghai received another telegram from Hong Kong stating that from July 1st, both silver bars and coins would be completely banned from being landed. The various reports heard are recorded below:

Rushing to Transport National Currency - Since the Hong Kong government announced the ban on Mexican silver dollars and limited each person to bringing no more than fifty dollars into the country, exchange houses in Shanghai changed to purchasing Yuan silver coins for transport to Hong Kong. Since last week, news came that Hong Kong merchants telegraphed saying that from the 7th, the Hong Kong authorities would also ban Yuan coins from entering. A group of Hakka people purchasing foreign rice began buying large quantities of Yuan coins in Shanghai from June 23rd, entrusting European and American postal ships to transport them to Hong Kong. Each ship was loaded with up to one million dollars to Hong Kong. The most transported was last week, stopping only on the day the report was filed. Even if Shanghai allows exports from today, unloading will not be allowed upon arrival in Hong Kong.

Refusal to Unload Large Bars - Large bars of American silver transported to Shanghai were rerouted to Hong Kong for temporary storage after being banned from being unloaded in Shanghai last month, in order to find ways to transport them into the interior. Yesterday, reliable information was received that the Hong Kong government no longer allows the unloading of American silver in Hong Kong. The banks decided to reroute the unloading to Singapore for storage. For example, the 789 American silver bars transported to Shanghai by a certain American ship the day before yesterday were rejected by the Jianghai Customs and have now been reloaded on the original ship and sent to Singapore.

Huge Amounts of Silver Rushed Out - Yesterday, a major British bank in Shanghai, in response to the implementation of the Hong Kong ban order on July 1st, rushed to declare a large quantity of silver bars, totaling 2,039 bars, for export yesterday so that they could be transported on the closing ship of June 30th and unloaded upon arrival in Hong Kong. The bank completed the formalities at 2 PM and transferred the silver to a connecting ship on the Bund of Hankou Road. This is the last batch of large silver bars from Shanghai to Hong Kong.

Shipping Silver to India - Shanghai has an excess of silver reserves. In order to adjust the financial situation, the banks previously shipped 4,000 large silver bars to India. Today, a second batch of silver is being exported, also to Calcutta, India, totaling a huge amount of 1.94 million taels. Another 20 boxes are being shipped to Singapore. The silver was loaded onto the ship at the Customs Wharf yesterday afternoon.

Shanghai Municipal Land Bureau Measures the Tangqiao District 153

Plots of Land in the Sixteenth and Seventeenth Maps of the Twenty-Fourth Bao and Second District

The Shanghai Municipal Land Bureau issued a proclamation yesterday to start measuring the land plots in the Sixteenth and Seventeenth Maps of the Twenty-Fourth Bao and Second District of the Tangqiao District, stating: "Proclamation regarding the Bureau currently starting to measure the land plots in the Sixteenth and Seventeenth Maps of the Twenty-Fourth Bao and Second District of the Tangqiao District. All property owners should pay attention to the following items: (1) The land guards will distribute filling-out forms to the property owners. Each property owner should truthfully fill in the forms within ten days after receiving them and have the land guards collect and submit them to the first measurement team of the Bureau or have the property owners send them directly to the measurement team. (2) Those who have not received the filling-out forms due to the property owner's address being unknown can directly submit them to the Bureau or the first measurement team. (3) If property owners cannot fill in the field list name and mu division due to the field list being mortgaged, they should promptly copy it from the mortgagee and not postpone it. (4) When the land of each household is measured, the property owner must, together with the land guard, clearly indicate the boundaries to the surveyor or pre-appoint a representative to the site to indicate the boundaries; otherwise, the Bureau will only rely on the land guard's instructions. If any errors or disputes occur in the future, the property owner will be responsible. The above four items are related to the property owners' consolidation of property rights. Please pay special attention to this proclamation."

Twenty-Eighth Time

Except for the part used by various banks and shops, which will be inspected separately according to the original method, this inspection of the interbank part is as follows: The amount issued by the bank itself and used by interbanks is 94,150,287.85 yuan. The amount of reserve funds for exchange coupons of the bank and interbanks is 94,150,287.85 yuan, including 57,980,216.11 yuan in cash reserves and 36,170,071.74 yuan in guarantee reserves. The above two items, with cash reserves accounting for 60% and guarantee reserves accounting for 40%, were all checked correctly. In accordance with Rule 5, this formal report is hereby made on June 29, 1920, by Xu Kan, Director of the Currency Department of the Ministry of Finance; Wang Yansong, representative of the Shanghai Special Municipality Chamber of Commerce Organization Committee; Qin Runqing; Sun Jingxi and Wu Weiru, representatives of the Shanghai Bankers Association; Tian Qiyuan and Chen Zixun, representatives of the Shanghai Money Trade Association; Tang Shoumin and Chuan Hongshui, representatives of the coupon-receiving banks and shops; Li Jue, Zhou Zongliang, Ye Zhuotang, and Yu Jiqing, representatives of the directors and supervisors of the Bank of China; and Accountant Wang Zikang."

British Police Station Interrogated Two Indians Yesterday 156

Continued Interrogation Tomorrow

The Wenhui Newspaper reports that this morning (30th), the British Police Court heard a case against two Indians. One, Pusin, 35 years old, makes a living by lending money. He was arrested for inciting Indians after being dismissed from his position as an Indian prisoner guard at the Ward Road Prison for striking on Saturday. The British Consulate requested that if the British Consul did not grant their request, they would set fire to the consulate, committing a crime against public safety. The other, Sabulanxin, 27 years old, was charged with distributing inflammatory leaflets on Jing'an Temple Road on Sunday while serving as a doorman Indian prisoner guard. The Indian community in Shanghai is paying close attention to both cases, and the courtroom was full of onlookers. After the court session began, Pusin was interrogated first. Lawyer Bishi Hua clarified the case and the Western police chief Lusi testified about the arrest. Because the defendant wanted to hire a lawyer, the hearing was postponed to Wednesday. Then the second Indian was interrogated, also with lawyer Bishi Hua prosecuting and Western police Lusi testifying that at 8:30 last night, he was driving past the Carlton Theater on Jing'an Temple Road and saw the defendant distributing leaflets to Chinese and foreign people and British soldiers. He immediately stopped the car and tailed the suspect until the defendant noticed him and threw the leaflets and the small flag he was carrying into the sky. He then chased and arrested him and ordered Chinese police to pick up the leaflets and flags, totaling sixty to seventy copies of "A Letter to Indian Compatriots" and thirteen copies of "India Never Had a Gandhi" printed in Chinese and English, as well as a flag of the Indian National Congress. He then brought the defendant to the police station. After the magistrate took Lusi's testimony, he ordered the defendant to be detained and await continued interrogation on Wednesday.

Ningbo Compatriot Association 157

Fundraising Meeting Closed Yesterday

Yi Wei Team Emerges as Dark Horse

The Ningbo Shanghai Compatriot Association held its fifth fundraising announcement and closing ceremony yesterday. Wang Boyuan, the general captain; Zhang Jiguang and Hong Yanbin, the general staff; Mao Ziren; team captains Wang Dongyuan, Zhu Yewei, Mao Heyuan; and more than 600 team members were present. Fang Jiaobo was publicly elected as chairman. After performing the ceremony, the chairman announced the opening of the meeting. The general captain and general staff gave speeches. The Shengping team was the first to open, scoring 400 points, hoping to win first place. The Ziren and Jiaobo teams added points one after another, competing. The Yewei team, led by Zhu Yewei, a Chinese overseas Chinese in Singapore, emerged as a dark horse, breaking through the ranks with 600 points. The Shengping team also showed no weakness and tried to counterattack. The atmosphere at the meeting was tense. As a result, the Yewei team won first place with 1,100 points, the Shengping team was second with 1,000 points, the Ziren team was third with 602 points, the Jiaobo team was fourth with 519 points, and the Zipei team was fifth with 375 points. The general team awarded 100 points to the first team, 60 points to the second team, 40 points to the third team, 30 points to the fourth team, and 20 points to the fifth team. Then the micro-fundraising announcement was held (combining the scores of the five announcements, the first primary school team raised 3,205 points, the second Jiaobo team 1,841 points, the third Shengping team 1,348 points, the fourth Yewei team 1,200 points, and the fifth Ziren team 1,142 points. It is reported that a total of 32,655 points were raised (the rest is omitted). The result exceeded the predetermined goal by more than one-tenth. Given the recent situation in Shanghai, this achievement shows the extraordinary enthusiasm of the two people for protecting the compatriot community.

Telegram Received by the Sino-Foreign Relief Association Branch

The Shanghai Sino-Foreign Relief Association recently received a telegram from the Dengfeng County Relief Branch, stating: "Respectfully replying, we have received your letter in which you stated that Dengfeng has suffered another catastrophic hailstorm. How can the surviving people endure this? Hearing this from afar, we are extremely concerned. Our association has always been responsible for soliciting relief funds in Henan Province, which have been successively remitted to the Sino-Foreign Relief Association in Kaifeng, Henan, for distribution in accordance with the board of directors' decision. Please report the recent disaster situation in detail to the association. Therefore, in addition to promptly reporting in detail, we are obligated to reply by telegram. Our association does not dare to be rashly disrespectful, but we are deeply concerned that the corpses are piled high, and we fear that the survivors will be destitute. Our responsibilities are closely related, and we should earnestly seek relief. The hailstorm in Dengfeng this time can be said to be the extreme point. The disaster is ten thousand times worse. This urgent relief effort can be said to be ten thousand times more critical. Every household in the disaster area has long been without food, and everyone is crying for help. After investigation, there are indeed 18,767 households and 98,164 disaster victims. 1,209 qing and 9 mu of wheat fields were completely destroyed, and 1,613 houses were destroyed. Chairman of the Branch, Zhang Jingxuan, respectfully bows."

Business Prohibition Bureau Seriously Handles Trademark Exclusive Rights 162

The Trademark Bureau approved the presentation of Xi Yuchang, the lawyer representing Delong Cigarette Factory, stating: "It is known that the trademark of the business, the Flag Beauty brand, has a picture of a half-length woman facing to the left, with a flower in her black hair, wearing a deep blue dress and a light blue vest. The background is a golden convex shape with red and blue dotted lace on both sides. Outside the lace is a golden flower pattern in the shape of a peacock tail, surrounded by a swastika frame, in which a line of red Western characters is written. There are other characters at the top and bottom (the pattern on the back is very complicated, so I won't list them here). The steel seal pattern printed on the cigarette sticks is a full-length light blue half-length woman without flowers in her left hair, surrounded by a golden flower pattern of similar shape in an oval circle, with blue and golden Western characters written in a line below. Compared with the original picture of the registered trademark of the Flag Beauty brand of the business, they are very different. However, at first glance, it is almost the same as the Beautiful brand joint trademark registered by Huacheng Tobacco Company. Therefore, when Huacheng Tobacco Company applied for banning, the bureau immediately ordered the business to quickly delete it. However, the business made a big announcement, claiming that the steel seal pattern on the cigarette sticks was made according to the registered trademark. Now, we are about to issue a strict order to inquire. According to the presentation and defense, in addition to sophistry and strong arguments that the steel seal pattern is not similar to the Beautiful brand of Huacheng Tobacco Company, it also said that there is no difference between the woman in the steel seal pattern and the registered trademark of the Flag Beauty brand. The business stated on one hand that the steel seal pattern was made according to the registered trademark of the Flag Beauty brand, and on the other hand, said that there was no difference from the registered trademark of the Flag Beauty brand. The business has already changed the pattern of its registered trademark to imitate and use it. According to Article 19, Paragraph 1 of the Trademark Law, it should be revoked immediately. Now, in accordance with the provisions of Paragraph 3 of the same article, the Trademark Bureau's punishment of revocation specified in Paragraph 1 should be notified to the trademark exclusive right holder or its agent sixty days in advance. This approval is hereby issued for notification."

Huang and Lu are in Love 166

Lu Genrong Declared Not Guilty

Lu Genrong Temporarily Still Detained

Release Must Wait for Confirmation

The case of Huang and Lu's love affair has been widely publicized in society. The issue of Lu Genrong's two criminal charges of seduction and theft has been appealed to the Supreme Court twice, and the re-trial procedures have been quite complicated. It was not until yesterday (30th) that he was declared not guilty. Lu has been detained since June 23rd of the lunar calendar in the summer of 1928. Later, the Wuxian Local Court sentenced him to two years for seduction. His lover, Huang Huiru, stated that the love between the two was with her consent. According to the new law, Lu had no reason to be convicted. She stayed in Wuxia and hired lawyer Song Mingxun to appeal to the High Court. Unexpectedly, the High Court changed the sentence to four years for the crime of intending to commit adultery and abduction. Later, he again ran around trying to appeal to the Supreme Court. As a result, Lu was changed to the crime of aiding and abetting theft, with a sentence of two years. At that time, Huang suddenly died of postpartum depression, extinguishing her beauty. If Huiru is dead, Genrong finally achieved the goal of being declared not guilty. Huiru, if she knew in the afterlife, would be able to rest in peace. However, even if Lu's freedom is restored, he should have a feeling that a beauty will not return. Yesterday (30th) at 2 PM, Zhao Zhengdang, the acting presiding judge of the Criminal Third Court of the High Court, accompanied by judges Fang Wen and Zheng Zhiguo, prosecutor Jin Henian, and secretary Yi Xuheng, ascended the seat in the first courtroom. As usual, they asked for names and ages and then announced the main text of the judgment: "In the case of Lu Genrong of Wuxian appealing against the theft, the part of the judgment concerning Lu Genrong's crime of theft is revoked. Lu Genrong is not guilty of the part of the theft charged." He also instructed that after his release from prison this time, he must be law-abiding and not do evil. Lu Genrong requested to be released on bail in court. Judge Zhao replied that he would wait until the case file was sent to the Prosecutor's Office. If the prosecutor does not appeal, he can be released, it is said. After the ruling, Lu was returned to custody. At that time, Lu's father, Huiqing, and Lu's cousin, Tang Yixian, went to the former Wuxian Third Prison Branch to visit Lu Genrong. He has been in custody for two years and has been in contact with other criminals, and he is full of new terms, it is said. Yesterday's debate concluded.

Liu Siqiao's Tragic Death Case 167

Complete Despair of Reconciliation Between the Two Parties

Pan Shiju Denies Negligence

Sentencing Scheduled for the Morning of the 5th

Pan Shiju, the son of Pan, the compradore of the Bureau of Works, drove his newly purchased car at high speed on the Great West Road on April 7th and crashed into Dr. Liu Siqiao, killing him. Liu's wife, Li, hired lawyer Jiang Yiping to first sue him for murder in the Special District Local Court, and then withdrew the lawsuit and filed a civil lawsuit requesting Pan Shiju to compensate for the loss of 60,000 yuan. The summons and order to go out for reconciliation have been recorded in this newspaper. However, although Pan Shiju killed Liu in the crash, he denied that it was his fault, resulting in complete despair of reconciliation. Yesterday morning, Judge Xu Wenrong continued the trial. The defendant presented two witnesses, one was Pan's chauffeur, Wang A'bao, and the other was Zhu Hesheng, the rickshaw puller of the rickshaw Liu was riding at the time. The testimony was unfavorable to the plaintiff, saying that if Liu Siqiao had jumped off the north side of the rickshaw he was riding in, he would not have been hit by the car. However, he jumped off from the south side, resulting in the disaster, and so on. Then the debate began. According to the plaintiff's lawyer, Jiang Yiping, if the defendant's car had not hit the rickshaw Liu was riding in and shaken Liu out of the car, Liu would never have jumped out of the rickshaw by himself. Even if Liu jumped out by himself, if the defendant's car had not been speeding and chasing the car in front, causing him to take the wrong route and hit Liu's car, Liu would not have jumped out. Therefore, the defendant's responsibility for negligence is difficult to shirk. Today's two witnesses, one is the defendant's own chauffeur, who will naturally protect his master, and the other is the rickshaw puller of the deceased, but his rickshaw was damaged in the crash and repaired by the defendant. Therefore, this person's testimony is not directly bought with money, but indirectly has a financial relationship, so it is not worth trusting. The defendant's car is insured and his family is rich. The amount of compensation requested by the plaintiff is well within his ability to bear. The deceased's average monthly income was 800 yuan, and he was only over 30 years old. Calculating with a lifespan of 60 years, the loss is not extravagant. The defendant Pan Shiju's two lawyers replied that the negligence was on Liu Siqiao's part and said that if the defendant must be found to have negligence and the amount of compensation, it cannot be as the plaintiff requested. They also cited the recent case of Shen Pengnian, the former Director of Education of Jiangsu Province, being killed by a car as a ratio, saying that the driver in that case should bear more responsibility for negligence than in this case, and the result was only an order to compensate about 6,000 yuan. The judge then announced the end of the debate and scheduled the sentencing for the morning of July 5th.

Wu Jian Guang and Others Accused 168

Plaintiff Yu Qingyu presented substantial evidence, accusing Wu and others of using deceptive words to confuse the public and obtain money through fraud. In Shanghai, those who engage in divination and astrology are as numerous as the stars in the Ganges River, but the most renowned are Wu Jianguang, Chai Wenzhong, Wang Yonghai, and Wang Zhenhai. Among them, Wu is particularly known for his extensive supernatural powers, rarely matched. However, there has never been any instance of requesting their prohibition. Now, like a thunderclap, these four individuals are jointly accused of using deceptive words to confuse the public and obtain money through fraud. The plaintiff requests the Special District Local Court to shut them down, summon them for questioning, and impose penalties. The plaintiff is Yu Qingyu, a standing committee member of the Second District Tenth Branch. His complaint is roughly as follows:

Complaint Content: It has long been prohibited to use superstition to harm people, but unexpectedly, under this clear and bright sky, there are blind people assuming the role of fortune-telling houses, defrauding women of large sums of money. The facts are recorded below: (1) Blind people establish fortune-telling houses using their status as disabled individuals, and their fortune-telling and divination are not too excessive, so although it is known that they use superstition to confuse people, strict prohibitions have not been imposed. Initially, it was not expected that there would be such a significant hidden agenda. (2) The hidden agenda of the blind people: Whenever women come to them for fortune-telling, they inquire about their addresses and family situations. If men or women are having affairs, they say they are afflicted by the "Peach Blossom Star"; if they have no children, they say they are afflicted by the "Heavenly Dog Star"; if they are losing property, they say they are afflicted by the "White Tiger Star"; if they are sick, they say they are afflicted by the "Mourning Gate Star," "Hanging Guest Star," or "Hemp-Wearing Star." Women who fall for their tricks are then ordered to hire a number of Taoist priests to perform rituals using various fake talismans, stepping on the Big Dipper formation, and striking gongs and cymbals. The cost for one day is as high as hundreds of gold pieces, or at least dozens of yuan. Wu Jianguang on Nanjing Road, Chai Wenzhong on North Nicheng Bridge (after Wenzhong's death, his two sons Chai Caifa and Chai Caigao took over), Wang Yonghai, and Wang Zhenhai on South Chengda Lane each earn hundreds or thousands of yuan daily, which outsiders are unaware of. (3) Initially, party members thought that as disabled individuals, they should be given some leeway until the government can help them solve their food, clothing, and housing problems. However, they have become increasingly brazen, so it was necessary to go undercover and obtain evidence of Chai Wenzhong and others defrauding with the blind people using明眼人 (people who can see) for sixteen yuan and six jiao, and evidence of employing blind people to set up scams for one hundred and seventy-six yuan. In addition to the resolution by the Ninth Executive Committee of the Second District Tenth Branch to submit a request to the higher authorities to consult with the Chinese and foreign concessions to strictly prohibit them, a lawsuit is also filed with your court to recover the losses from the fraud and punish them according to the law. (Reason) Using deceptive words to confuse the public and obtain money through fraud is a violation of specific laws. It is the duty of this party to eliminate superstition and absolutely not allow these people to engage in deception and fraud again, bringing shame to the party's rule and the community. (Objective) Please arrest the defendants and reserve the right for the victims to file private lawsuits. Please also announce within the territory that if the above circumstances are encountered, the public may report, arrest, and send them to court at any time to eliminate superstition and prevent them from falling into their tricks again.

Court's Interrogation: Upon receiving the complaint, the court immediately issued summonses to the defendants Wu Jianguang and others, ordering them to appear in court for questioning in the past few days. After receiving the summonses, only Wang Yonghai hired a lawyer to argue that he was forced to make a living in this way, and that there are hundreds of people in Shanghai who do this, and even foreigners in Shanghai who engage in mentalism and palmistry. Why not prosecute them one by one? Furthermore, bookstores sell books on astrology, feng shui, and talismans, all of which are forms of superstition. Incense offerings and prayers are not prohibited in temples and Taoist monasteries. Why is there preferential treatment? The plaintiff filed a public lawsuit because Taoist He Yaokun reported them out of personal grudges, which is discriminatory. Furthermore, the plaintiff is a loyal party member and could have openly prohibited them. Why did they have to go undercover and lie, using deceptive means to make people fall into error? This is akin to punishing without prior instruction. He requests that the case be dismissed and reserves the right to file a private lawsuit for the defendants' losses. Yesterday morning, Judge Feng Shide opened the court. Wu Jianguang claimed illness and did not attend, sending lawyer Ye Fikang as his representative. Only the two Wangs appeared in court, and the Chai brothers did not attend. Judge Feng first interrogated Yu Qingyu, who stated that Wang Wenhai was a fortune-teller hired by Chai Caifa and Caigao. Then, lawyer Ye stated that the part of the complaint against Wu Jianguang did not specify the legal articles or how the fraud was committed. The plaintiff's lawyer then stated that the prosecution was based on Article 363 of the Criminal Law. Yu then stated that on June 13, he went to Chai Wenzhong's fortune-telling house, pretending that a Mr. Chen was ill and had come for divination. Wang Yonghai performed the divination, and the result was very ominous. When asked if there was a way to perform a ritual to ward off the evil, Wang said that it would require two days of prayer and a cost of one hundred and sixty yuan. He was asked to open an account, and he immediately demanded sixteen yuan, which was given to him. Wang Zhenhai specializes in selling fake scriptures. His wife once bought the "Five Thunder Gods Mantra" and other scriptures from him, costing five yuan. Last year, his wife went to Wu Jianguang for divination because she had no children. Wu said that he was afflicted by the "Heavenly Dog Star" and that the child had been eaten. He said that a ritual must be performed to have a chance of having children. The method of performing the ritual was to conduct a Taoist ceremony for one day, and he told his wife not to let him know. His wife was fooled and spent one hundred and thirty-four yuan to conduct a Taoist ceremony for one day and obtained a paper talisman to ward off evil in the house. He only found out about this now. Wang Yonghai denied receiving sixteen yuan from the plaintiff. Wang Zhen also stated that he did not sell scriptures. Judge Feng then adjourned the hearing to a later date at Rue Massenet.

Terrifying Male Corpse 169

A letter to the police was found near the corpse, stating that the deceased was Zhang Mingguen. It appears to be a case of murder due to uneven distribution of spoils.

At around 2:30 AM yesterday morning, a patrol officer of the French Concession Police Department discovered an unidentified male corpse lying in a pool of blood on the roadside in front of a foreign house at No. 41 Rue Massenet. The officer immediately reported to the Chief of the French Concession Police Department in Lujiawan, who dispatched Chinese and foreign detectives to investigate. The deceased was found to be approximately thirty years old, with a long face, a monk's bald head, no hat, wearing a white cotton short shirt and trousers with a white dirty shirt underneath, a white silk waistband, light gray silk socks, and black leather shoes. He had three gold teeth inlaid in his mouth. He had been shot twice, one bullet entering from the outer end of the left eyebrow and penetrating the back of the head, and the other entering from below the right rib under the nipple and lodging in the back without penetrating. A letter was found in his chest pocket with "To the Police Department" written on the envelope, specifying the deceased's name as Zhang Mingguen. It was from this that the deceased's name was known (this letter appeared to have been inserted by the murderer after Zhang was killed). According to the investigation by the detectives, residents nearby reported that a car was seen passing by around 1:30 AM, followed by several gunshots. However, they did not know any details. The detectives took the letter back to the police station to report to the chief, who then notified Tongren Fuyuantang to send undertakers to carry the body to the coroner's office. No belongings of the deceased were found. Yesterday morning, the police department sent someone to the coroner's office to photograph the body, and a lead bullet was found protruding from the back of the body, with the bullet head flattened. The detective took it to the police department for storage. Subsequently, the Criminal Division reported to the French Court, and Judge Zhu Cheng arrived at the coroner's office at 11:30 AM at noon to conduct the examination. He sat in the official position, and the detectives reported the previous situation and presented the letter and lead bullet. After reviewing the evidence, Judge Zhu determined that the deceased had indeed been shot to death. Since no belongings of the deceased were found, Tongren Fuyuantang was ordered to prepare a coffin for burial and placement in the altar, awaiting family members to claim the body and awaiting the police department to arrest the murderer for interrogation. According to general speculation at the time, it was said that it was probably a case of internal conflict and killing among comrades due to uneven distribution of spoils, resulting in extreme poverty.

Jing Fengxiang Attempts Suicide in Pudong 170

Money is exhausted, resources are depleted. Unable to make a living, it's too tragic.

At around 7 PM the night before last, the No. 4 ferry at Chunjiang Wharf in Pudong loaded over twenty passengers at the New Customs Wharf on the opposite bank and sailed back to Pudong. Unexpectedly, when the boat reached the center of the river, a middle-aged man took advantage of others' inattention and suddenly jumped into the river to commit suicide. Fortunately, he was rescued by the crew and did not drown. The captain, Qian Zhisheng, immediately sent him to the Water Police Station. According to his statement, his name is Jing Fengxiang, thirty years old, from Shaoxing, currently residing at No. 147, Lane 6, Zhen'anli, Gonghe Road, Zhabei. He has joined the Chinese Nationalist Party as a member, and his party certificate number is Zhe No. 5323. In 1925, he worked as a messenger in the Shaoxing Police Bureau in Zhejiang for quite some time. In February 1927, when the National Revolutionary Army arrived in Zhejiang, he worked as an assistant in the dispatch office of the Zhejiang Provincial Party Headquarters. In June 1929, he lost his job and brought his wife to Shanghai with the intention of seeking other employment. Later, he met a friend surnamed Xu, who was a bodyguard for someone in the French Concession. He asked Xu to find him any job to make a living temporarily. Unfortunately, his luck was not good, and Xu's older sister suddenly passed away in his hometown. Xu immediately returned home to attend the funeral and did not return to Shanghai until October of that year. Because it had been too long, he was fired by his employer and could no longer take care of his employment problem, causing the couple to wander around until now. All his savings have been completely exhausted. Even the several sets of Western-style clothes that he brought to Shanghai have been pawned. He has exhausted all means and has no way to think. On June 26th of this month, his friend Cao Jingui mentioned that the Public Security Bureau was recruiting police officers for the Fifth Squadron. He went to apply for the examination, and his eyesight, hearing, strength, and physical examination were all rated as A. Later, for the written test, he still remembered one question: "Why are you taking this exam?" He answered, "We are taking the exam to seek the happiness of the Party and the country for the country, to protect the security of the local people and business community for the people, and to seek a place to live for ourselves." Many of the examinees did not know how to read, so he helped them answer. The results of the examination showed that he could not find a guarantor to provide a guarantee, so he could not find a job. Seeing others being selected one after another, he did not get his wish. The most painful thing was that when he went to take the exam, he still borrowed one yuan from a friend, saying that it would be used as capital for doing a small business. Now the money has been used up, and he really has no face to see his friend. He is currently facing the end of his resources and has no choice but to commit suicide by jumping into the river. His words were so tragic that one could not bear to hear them. The police chief comforted him with a few words and ordered the detectives to bring his wife, Ms. Chen, to take him home that night.

Defendant appeals the sentence. Hou Genbao, residing in Tanziwan Guanlong, Zhabei, had an affair with his cousin Guan Caidi and, in order to seize the property of his uncle Guan Liukun, buried his cousin Guan Maoda alive, causing his death. Hou Genbao declared in court that he did not accept the verdict. The judge ordered him to appeal to the High Court within ten days and ordered him to be returned to custody.

Page 16

Parisian Dancer Huang Baiying

The Truth About Suicide 172

Recently, the Paris dance hall on Jing'an Temple Road moved its business to West Shanghai due to the summer heat. A dancer named Huang Baiying suddenly committed suicide by swallowing sleeping pills the other day. The situation was briefly reported previously, but the truth was not clear. Now, after a detailed investigation by reporters, the truth has been revealed as follows:

Dancer's Family Background: Huang Baiying is from Guangdong, and is currently nineteen years old. Huang was originally from a wealthy family and studied at a university in Guangdong, excelling in calligraphy and literature. However, her father was not good at managing the business, and the family's fortunes declined. When she was sixteen years old, her parents passed away one after another. Baiying was lonely and helpless, and had few siblings, resulting in the bankruptcy of the entire family. Because it was difficult for a lone girl to maintain a living in her hometown, a relative took her to Shanghai, seeing her beauty, and she lived with a friend. She then learned to dance and entered the Great Eastern as a low-ranking dancer. Because of her gentle nature, she got along well with her colleagues.

A Flower Fallen into the Mire: After Huang Baiying became a dancer at the Great Eastern, she devoted herself to studying dance. However, modern dance halls are opportunities for good girls to fall. Baiying, influenced by what she saw and heard, had to transform from a dignified woman into a charming and seductive figure. At this time, a dance patron named Tong Sanmao, nicknamed "Long-legged Tong," saw Baiying's beauty and wanted to take a bite of forbidden fruit. He planned to seduce her. Huang, as a dancer, had no status to speak of and willingly complied.

Love in the Battlefield: Tong Sanmao was the young owner of a candy company in Tilanqiao, Hongkou. However, he liked to indulge in pleasure and willingly associated with degenerate people. As a result, his father and brother did not pay attention to him and allowed him to mess around outside. Baiying was favored by Tong Sanmao, but women are mostly fickle. Over time, she became tired of him. In addition, Tong often acted like he was her husband, and there were often arguments. The manager of the Great Eastern saw that Baiying had this affair and that it was not good for the overall situation, so he wanted to suspend her dance business. This was learned by the Paris dance hall, which recruited her as their own.

Turmoil in the Sea of Jealousy: After the dancer Huang Baiying joined Paris, her love with Tong slightly diminished. A college student named Zhang often came to Paris to dance. Seeing that Baiying was skilled in dancing and knowing that she understood English and spoke it fluently while embracing her, he considered her to be his soulmate in the dance hall. This news reached Tong's ears, inevitably arousing his jealousy, regarding Zhang as his rival. He then spread defamatory words in front of the crowd, insisting that Baiying must marry him.

Rivals Meet: Zhang, since falling in love with the dancer Baiying, frequented Paris every night, greatly enjoying himself. Tong knew about their secret actions, so on the evening of the 28th, he also went to the Paris dance hall. Baiying greeted him. Zhang, seeing Tong, feared that he would be unfavorable to him, so he slipped away after a while. Zhang's friend Fang knew the inside story and wanted to mediate between the two, asking Baiying to dance with Tong several times. The three sat at the same table, talking about other things. When the dance was over and the hall was dismissed, Fang invited Tong and Baiying to go out together.

Forced Killing in a Hotel: Baiying knew that Tong had bad intentions, but her claims were of no avail. She told Ge Songxian, the assistant manager of Paris, that Tong and Fang had invited her to go out, and she didn't know if she could go. Ge, not knowing the details, replied that there was no danger and she could go. Baiying then boarded a car with them, heading straight to Wusong for a ride. When they reached Wusong, Tong took out a metal rod from the car, intending to hit Fang. Fang also argued strongly. Tong then drove the car back to Shanghai, dropping Fang off in the middle of Baek Road. He then went straight to the Cangzhou Hotel in West Shanghai, opening another room. After closing the door, he took out a package of sleeping pills, ordering Baiying to swallow them, saying that if Baiying wanted to love Zhang, he would deal with her in an appropriate manner.

Poisoning En Route: Baiying, at this critical moment, was like Wang Lianying, and Tong insisted that she write a letter to Zhang to cut off their relationship. Baiying had no choice but to swallow twelve sleeping pills. Tong, knowing that she had taken poison, feared that it would implicate him, and that his name would be written on the record of the incident. At this time, he immediately took Baiying out, intending to go to Baiying's residence at No. 65 Wanli Lane, Lafayette Road, in the French Concession. Unexpectedly, the poison had already taken effect en route. Tong then sent Baiying to the Baolong Hospital by rickshaw. After several diagnoses by the doctor, she is now able to speak a little. There are fears that Huang and Fang will propose serious charges. Baek Road

Leaping from Building Death Case Verdict 175

Han Fuguo shouldn't enter other people's homes.

The verdict is that he will be detained in the West Prison for one month.

Han Fuguo, from Jiangbei, came to Shanghai from his hometown with his wife Wu in the year before last to make a living. They lived together in the Zhabei area. Han worked outside, and Wu did sewing outside. The poor couple depended on each other, lived a hard life, and their relationship was still relatively harmonious. Initially, they lived in peace with no differences. Unexpectedly, starting last year, Han became lazy and unemployed, relying on his wife's needlework to make a living, and often asked Wu for money to use. If he was not satisfied, he would beat and scold her. As a result, the two developed animosity, and Wu regretted marrying him. She became familiar with Xu Funian (who works as a ticket collector at the Albert Road Powerball Stadium) from Yangzhou and eloped with him in September of last year, living with Xu in a pavilion-style building at No. 3 Shenshengli, Qianjiatang, in the French Concession, living like husband and wife. However, the secret was discovered by Han Fuguo, who, on the morning of the 24th of last month, brought a crowd to the place to catch them in the act. Wu heard the sound and woke Xu up, and she fled to the home of a Zhang family next door to take refuge. Xu hid in the room of Yan in the front building. Han used a bamboo ladder to climb to the upper floor to search, and then tore open the wall of the front building, intending to enter and catch them in the act before stopping. Xu Funian, with no escape, in a moment of desperation, jumped out of the window, attempting to escape. Unexpectedly, he injured his vital parts and fell to the ground unconscious. The patrolling police officer from 426 arrived and arrested Han, along with Wu, and brought them to the police station. At the same time, the injured person was sent to the hospital. He died due to his serious injuries. The details have been previously recorded. Yesterday, the police station sent all the people involved to the French Court for questioning. First, the police chief reported the previous situation. Han Fuguo confessed that his wife took their one-year-old child out to work as a helper on September 16th of last year and never returned until he saw a civilian in the vegetable market a few days ago. He followed her and learned that she was living with the deceased in Shenshengli. Therefore, he went to call his wife home in the morning. He didn't know how Xu Funian, feeling guilty, jumped out of the window, and it wasn't because he was forced by the civilian to seek forgiveness. The Chinese and Western judges sentenced the defendant Han Fuguo for improperly entering other people's residences and ordered him to be detained in the West Prison for one month as a warning to Wu and released Xu.

Ruffians Cause Trouble at Restaurant 177

Restaurant owner beaten by mob

The Xieyuguan Restaurant, recently opened on Oujia Road, Shanghai East, had its opening day (the 27th) the day before yesterday and was doing quite well. The next day at noon, a customer who looked like a ruffian entered the restaurant and took a seat. Cai Changfu, a waiter, thirty-four years old from Pudong, went forward to greet the customer attentively. The customer said to Cai that he needed two pieces of "miao rou" (a type of meat). After a short time, the meat was cooked and placed on the table. After inspecting it carefully, the customer complained that the meat was too fatty and needed to be replaced. Cai replied that there was no lean meat. The customer's face showed displeasure, and he threw the bowl on the table and left in a hurry. Cai, because the new store had just opened, wanted to settle the matter to avoid trouble and did not argue with him. Unexpectedly, at 8:30 PM last night, the customer led seven or eight tough-looking people, armed with axes, into the Xieyuguan without asking any questions. One person raised an axe and struck Cai Changfu on the head. Fortunately, Cai was very strong and used his right hand to block the axe, injuring his left wrist and causing blood to flow like a river. The others swarmed forward and started fighting. Cai also resisted despite his injuries, and his head was injured by a stool. A brawl ensued, with cups and plates scattered everywhere. Then, colleagues went out to call the police on duty, and the thugs scattered like birds and beasts. The main offender was arrested by the police and taken to the Third Sub-District of the Fifth District for investigation. The injured person was sent to Tongren Hospital by car for treatment.

Cao Zhaosun, twenty-four years old from the local area, residing in the Xizhuhuzhai area of Caojiadu, West Shanghai, worked as a tailor. He lost his parents at a young age and was an orphan with no support. He studied hard and grew up, being diligent and thrifty, and was highly respected by the villagers. In the previous year, he was engaged to a woman surnamed Mou through a matchmaker. Because of financial difficulties, they have not yet completed the marriage. He has been working diligently for two years, and has accumulated some savings. He has now chosen the sixth day of the tenth month of this year to get married. All the betrothal gifts and clothes have been prepared. Unexpectedly, yesterday morning at around 10 AM, Zhaosun, due to the hot weather, went to the nearby Zhuanbang with three or four neighbors to bathe and swim. They tried their best to salvage him, but he had already drowned and died. His nephew Cao Fugen carried the body back to establish an heir to inherit and prepare a coffin for burial. The villagers nearby all lamented and were saddened by this.

Mainland Newspaper Proofreader Catches Thief Barehanded 187

Liang Shanmei's Courage is Commendable. Liang Shanmei, an assistant proofreader at the Mainland Newspaper and a native of Guangdong, was on his way home from the newspaper office at around 4:00 AM the other morning. As he was walking along Huolun Mill Street in the French Concession, he saw a fellow villager, nicknamed "Old Guangdong," being robbed by a thief. Liang, seeing this injustice, bravely stepped forward to help. The thief immediately fled north to the intersection of Hubei Road and Guangdong Road, where he hid behind the door of a cigarette paper shop. Liang stopped and did not chase, but he had an idea. He took out a lighter box from his pocket, held it in his hand as if it were a gun, and pointed it at the thief, saying, "Come out and surrender, or I will shoot you!" The thief did not answer. Liang then pretended to fire the gun to scare him. The thief raised his hands to show that he dared not resist and surrendered. He did not realize that Liang was tricking him. The thief was later taken to the Songshan Road Police Station by the French police for interrogation. Mr. Fei Woli, the chief inspector of the French Concession Police Department, praised Liang Shanmei for his courage and intelligence in a special letter yesterday.

Just Laugh It Off - A Traveler 191

A: When you proposed to Miss C, did you kneel down in front of her?

B: I really wanted to kneel down to show my sincerity, but she was sitting on my lap.

Father: You must learn my skills to make a fortune, just like when you go to the bank to do business.

Son: May I ask what your skills are, Father, so that I can emulate them?

Father: In the past, I was the chief accountant at D Bank. I embezzled for three years before it was discovered. Do you think the skills I used to cover it up for those three years were great?

Student A: Westerners often say that Friday is an unlucky day, but I don't think so.

Student B: What reason do you have?

Student A: Because their greatest historical figures, such as Napoleon and Washington, were born on Sundays.

Student B: One general succeeds, and ten thousand bones wither. It's all because they were born on Fridays, so Friday is still unlucky after all.

A: Hey, why is your face so gloomy today, like a rainy day?

B: Don't mention rain. I suffered because of it. Yesterday, I bet five yuan with Lao Bing that it would definitely be rainy today, but it turned out to be neither rainy nor dry.

A Record of the Interesting United Graduation Ceremony of Municipal Middle Schools, By Yan Ye 192

The Shanghai Municipal Public and Private Middle Schools held a unified graduation examination starting from the 16th of this month. On the 25th, they held a joint graduation ceremony at the Penglai Grand Theatre in the North City and the Central Auditorium in the South City in the morning and afternoon. The grand occasion has already been reported in the newspapers. I will now record some interesting facts from the Penglai venue for the attention of Juan Weng.

Choosing the Far Over the Near: The venues for the united graduation ceremony were divided into two locations, north and south. The intention must have been for the schools in the South City to go to Penglai, and those in the North City to go to the Central Auditorium. Who knew it would not be so? The distribution method was to have students whose examination paper numbers were within 1200 go to Penglai to participate, and those above 1200 go to the Central Auditorium. The convenience of the students going back and forth, regardless of whether the school was in the north or south, was not considered at all. Therefore, on this day, the front seats were already occupied by students from the South City schools, who were more conveniently located. The students from the North City could only sigh and retreat to the back rows. It is said that the North City students suffered from choosing the far over the near. It was even more painful to arrive and not get a good seat.

Speeches with Different Styles: There were four speakers. Director Chen of the Education Bureau spoke eloquently for almost an hour, giving separate instructions on further education and employment, gesticulating and acting with extreme enthusiasm. The mayor's representative gave a gentle and calm speech, like a teacher lecturing in the classroom, gesticulating naturally. The two representatives of the school principals who delivered speeches, one was Mr. Pang of Junyi, and the other was Ms. Wang Xiaoying of Wuben. Mr. Pang started calmly and then became enthusiastic, like a clear breeze and beautiful sunshine gradually turning into a heavy rain and storm. Ms. Wang was good at Mandarin and long speeches. When she stepped onto the stage, the audience became quieter. She stood tall and upright, with her hands always behind her back. Her voice was clear, and her attitude was calm, giving people the feeling of taking a refreshing medicine after hearing Mr. Pang's enthusiastic and passionate speech.

The Most Enthusiastic Applause for Minli: The number of graduates from Minli was the largest among the schools. When the mayor's representative distributed graduation certificates, representatives from each school went forward to receive them. The applause was weak or even silent for schools with fewer students. When the master of ceremonies called out Minli, there was a burst of applause like thunder, deafening the ears. It was the same for Minli Girls' Middle School. The two schools are actually one and the same, and the brothers and sisters are congratulating each other.

The Honor of Young Fudan: Director Chen gave separate certificates to those who were ranked A in all subjects of the unified examination to encourage them. On this day, the most awardees were students from Youth and Fudan schools. Therefore, the sound of Youth and Fudan students was constantly heard, and the applause was more enthusiastic than when the certificates were given. When a student from Youth received the award, the master of ceremonies shouted that this was the first place in the junior high school unified examination. Everyone paid attention and applauded him. Later, Director Chen suddenly said that the report of the first place was wrong, and that only grades were assessed, not rankings, so there was no such thing as first, second, or third place. Thus, the student's first place was gained and then lost.

The Well-Behaved Bows of Female Students: All those who received certificates and awards had to bow twice to the person giving the award. Many male students bowed properly, but in the end, they were not as good as the female students, who were all respectful, standing straight and bending their bodies at a 90-degree angle. Also, because the female students had short hair, their hair would fall and cover their eyes when they bowed, and they would shake their heads when they stood up, which was also very interesting.

Trivial Records of the Xinghua Temple Fair, By Xu Xiaoting 193

Xinghua is a remote area in Jiangbei, and the people's superstitious customs are very strong. Although the national system has been reformed, the custom of welcoming gods and holding temple fairs in the middle of the fifth month of the lunar calendar still persists. The fair lasts for more than ten days, and the people waste time and money more than anything else. Now that the temple fair is approaching again, I will record some trivial news from the fair.

Precious Carvings: There are many rare items in the grand meeting. The most eye-catching is the hollow bamboo umbrella of the Jiangfu Society. The umbrella is hexagonal and completely made of hollow bamboo pieces inlaid together. It is said to have come from a famous craftsman in Jiading. The carvings are exquisite and the patterns are beautiful. At first glance, it looks like fine silk with paintings on it. The umbrella was originally made in ten pieces, but now it has been damaged and lost, leaving only six pieces.

Blue Sky, White Sun, and Red Earth: The gods welcomed at the temple fair are the City God, the Dutian, and the Dragon King. The fair dates are the 12th, 16th, and 20th days of the fifth month of the lunar calendar. The statue of the City God is white-faced, the Dutian is blue-faced, and the Dragon King is red-faced. This year, someone suggested that the City God's procession should be changed from the 12th to the 16th, and the Dutian should be brought forward to the 12th. This way, the three gods' processions would be in accordance with the saying "Blue Sky, White Sun, and Red Earth". However, local people followed the old custom, and the City God's date was ultimately not changed.

Competing for Novelty and Winning: The most eye-catching thing at the temple fair is the open-air sacrificial offering set up in various places. The sacrificial tables are set up on the streets and are very lavishly decorated, either with antiques and playthings or with exotic flowers and rare plants. In various colors, they all compete for novelty and winning. There are a total of one hundred and thirty or forty open-air sacrifices in the entire county.

The Judge Who is Used to Fighting: In addition to the open-air sacrifices, the most interesting thing at the temple fair is the judge. The judge was also at its peak with more than a hundred teams. The costumes are strange and different from the Zhong Jinshi in the paintings. The strongest of their solidarity is the ancient judge. The judge is completely gathered by brick and tile burners. Because of the large number of people, they often quarrel with other judges over the upper and lower positions when dancing on the road. Watching the judges fight in the large school field is also a novel highlight of the temple fair.

Taoist Priests and Nuns are Often Drowsy: Every time there is a meeting, Taoist priests and nuns all go to the temple to guard the night. The incense is curling and the Buddhist chants are noisy. Such a large temple is actually crowded with people, with no space to sit. General thieves often take advantage of their unpreparedness late at night to steal things. Because they stay up for three nights in a row, they are exhausted and mentally exhausted. They often suffer unexpected losses when they are drowsy, begging the gods for mercy, but the gods make them steal. The foolishness of the Taoist priests and nuns is pitiful and ridiculous.

Travel Notes of Hong Kong and Macau (Part 1), By Yin Zibai 194

Throughout my life, I have had a strong love for mountains and rivers. I have almost traveled all over the northeastern provinces, but I regret that I have not yet set foot in the southern border. A month ago, I was invited by my friend Zheng Wenbo to travel to Hong Kong and Macau for two weeks. So I bought a ticket on the Asia Queen, a ship owned by the Changxing Company with a tonnage of 16,400 tons, sailing at 20 nautical miles per hour. The distance from Hong Kong to Shanghai is 840 nautical miles, and it takes less than two days to reach Hong Kong. The journey was smooth and peaceful, and the ship was very comfortable. Upon landing, I temporarily stayed at the Dongshan Restaurant.

Hong Kong is located in the middle of the Asian coast, the largest commercial port in the Southeast Peninsula. The shipping routes are diverse and well-connected. The buildings are stacked on top of each other and the population is dense. Because it is a tax-free port, imported goods are re-exported from here. The British government has a Governor of Hong Kong to manage Chinese affairs.

Pomona College Confers Honorary Doctorate of Literature on Mei Lanfang, By Qi Rushan (Part 2) 195

After taking their seats, the president first gave the opening speech. After playing music and exchanging greetings, Dr. Luther Freeman, representing the entire faculty, gave a speech. He first spoke about the obligations and responsibilities of young people, and then said that now a young man has come from China. We can take this young man as an example. Who is this young man? It is Mr. Mei Lanfang. The first time I saw Mr. Mei's performance was "Chun Xiang Nao Xue." I found his comedic state so funny that I couldn't help but laugh. But when I met him backstage, I saw his calm and respectful air. I knew that he was a very great artist. Mr. Mei is famous all over the world, but he still treats older people with the respect of a disciple. This is the morality that our American youth lack the most, so we should take him as an example. The etiquette in China is originally like this, with fathers and brothers being called together and children and younger brothers being listed together. From this, we can know how young people should treat older people. Therefore, Chinese people always ask about age. If someone is older than oneself, then one should treat them with the respect of a disciple. It is said that if someone is ten years older, then treat them like an older brother. If someone is five years older, then follow them closely. This is also what we should take as an example. After the speech, Dr. Deng Qin left his seat and stood diagonally facing the president. The president also stood up. Dr. Deng Qin said, "Here is the great Chinese artist Mr. Mei Lanfang, whose artistic achievements are recognized worldwide and need no further elaboration. People only know that he is a great artist, but they do not know that he is also a great literary figure. In addition to acting, Mr. Mei has also devoted himself to the study of drama. He has been researching drama for more than twenty years and has created many works, contributing greatly to society. He has a library at home with many books, especially books on drama. Recently, he founded the Opera Academy in Nanjing and serves as its president. Mr. Mei has not only contributed to art but also to society and the world. I would like to introduce him to the president and ask the president to award Mr. Mei a doctorate of literature, because Mr. Mei's contributions to society are very much in line with the school's regulations for awarding degrees." After speaking, he asked Mr. Mei to stand up and introduced him to the president. The president said, "I have long heard of Mr. Mei's achievements in contributing to society, as mentioned by Dr. Deng Qin. On behalf of the faculty, I would like to award you a doctorate of literature." After speaking, he personally awarded the doctorate diploma. Then, two other doctors put the doctorate sash on Mr. Mei's shoulder. The audience applauded to congratulate him. Dr. Mei went on stage to give a speech, saying, "President, members of the board of directors, members of the faculty, students, and guests, I am very grateful to receive this honorary degree. This action shows the most profound international friendship towards us Chinese people. I am only a small representative traveling to your country to absorb new cultures and bring my own art to seek criticism from your scholars."

Wu, who is in charge of civilian administration, said that all government expenses are compensated by the opium monopoly and tobacco and alcohol taxes. It is said that the annual income is as high as 40 million. The weather is hot, and there is no frost or snow in winter. The wind is strong and the soil is floating, and it is often sunny and rainy. Locals say that all four seasons are like summer. A rain will turn into autumn. The customs are superstitious, and regardless of wealth or poverty, they all wear short jackets. However, there are also very novel ideas. For example, the recent promotion of the abolition of socks claims that arms can be exposed, and there is no need to wear socks on the feet. It is also economical and beautiful. I am afraid that people in Shanghai will also follow suit.

Zheng Junye said that the table salt in Hong Kong and Macau all comes from Annam. The annual sales are hundreds of thousands of dan, and the price is five cents per dan. Some come from Jinzhou and Taiwan, but the quality is rough and the taste is inferior. Chinese people are willing to eat domestic products. In the past, green salt was transported, but it was stopped halfway due to complicated procedures and high tax rates. After several years, not a single dan was imported. It is found that the domestic supply of table salt exceeds demand, and salt farmers in various provinces are struggling to survive due to unsalable products. The cost of green salt is less than thirty cents. If the government charges three cents per dan, as it does for salt exported to Japan, the cost will be only five cents to reach Hong Kong. Although the government only increases the salt tax by tens of thousands of gold, the salt farmers will export hundreds of thousands of dan, which is like being reborn from despair. Not only can domestic products be sold, but also people's livelihoods can be benefited. I hope that the salt administration will pay attention to it.

Looking at Hong Kong Island at night is like a lighthouse. There are cars up and down a mountain top, and there is a cable car shaped like a train. Its route is divided into four stations: Po Tak Road, Mei Road, Po Wan Road, and Gan Ni Di Road. Men's tickets are three cents each, and women's tickets are one cent each. Trams also have floors and are divided into four stations: 1. Causeway Bay to Kennedy Town, 2. Yue Garden to Kennedy Town, 3. Yue Garden to Sheung Wan Street, 4. Sheung Wan Street to Shau Kei Wan. The fare for each trip is one cent for first class and five cents for third class. Monthly tickets are ten yuan each for third class, half price. There are also public buses running on the Royal Pier, Repulse Bay, University Hall, Des Voeux Road, Garden Road, Kennedy Road, Bonham Road, Wan Chai, Stubbs Road, Wong Nai Chung Gap, and Auhua Bay.

Warmth in My Heart (2)(2)(4), By Bao Tianxiao 196

Chapter 12: A Farewell Banquet, Holding Flowers to Leave a Pretty Shadow; A Grand Garden Party, Comparing Tea to See Beautiful Postures

Yiyuan's silence and reticence always made Zuo Shichen think of Ruiyun's liveliness and innocence. Therefore, he really wanted to know some news about Ruiyun. It suddenly occurred to him that wasn't his great aunt asking him to call her successor, Hanyun? To know about Ruiyun, naturally, he had to call Hanyun. Hanyun was also a young teacher, and her personality was not unpleasant. She was a small bird dependent on others. When teased, her face would turn red. That kind of shy appearance was lovely. Zuo Shichen then went to call Hanyun to ask her about Ruiyun. She told Zuo Shichen everything she knew. She said that her older sister left on the twentieth day. They used a carriage to pick her up at the great aunt's house, not to pick her up for business. She said that the Zhang family hired a large official boat that was docked at the Guanyin Pavilion pier. They used a carriage to pick her up and take her to the boat, and they set sail that day. She said that A Jin accompanied her older sister. She said that she would be back in a week, and after returning, she would rest for a while and not sing in the hall. The great aunt said that A Jin had made enough money and would not sing in the hall anymore. She said that when her older sister left, she wore a newly made pink jacket and pink skirt, styled her hair, and wore flowers. She looked completely like a new bride. Our sisters also called a carriage to send her to the boat. She said that these few days, the great aunt was afraid that people would come to pester her, so she hid her older sister at the great aunt's mansion until the day before she left. Zuo Shichen knew about the great aunt that Hanyun mentioned. This was the little aunt's first founding minister, whose name was Yuan Manyun. Later, she redeemed herself, restored her freedom, and married someone, but she did not sever relations. She was like a kinsman. The reason why Ruiyun hid there was to avoid A Gui, Zhao Dakuaotou, and other people who wanted to bewitch her. Finally, Hanyun said, "If you see Second Young Master Zuo, ask him if he has picked up the photos from Baoji. It's best to ask you to print a few more. She also wants to give them to her little sisters." Zuo Shichen said, "The photos have already been picked up. As usual, there are only three. If you want to print more, I'll ask them to print more tomorrow. I don't know how many more you want to print." Hanyun said, "My older sister said she wanted to print half a dozen more." Zuo Shichen said, "Okay, I'll go print them tomorrow. Who should I give them to? Should I give them to you?" Hanyun said, "No, A Jin is coming soon. She has already told A Jin. She remembers clearly who each one is for among her sisters." Hanyun also pulled on Zuo Shichen's sleeve and said, "Second Young Master, you don't need all three. Give me one." Zuo Shichen said, "You can ask A Jin for one." Hanyun said, "She has six, and she has already given one to six people. Someone has already taken over a monk's share." Zuo Shichen said, "Okay, I'll give you one tomorrow."

Thin rice was also appraised by the bureau and then distributed to rice shops for sale. There are very few boats remaining in the lower reaches of the river, and the supply may be exhausted today. As no new boats have arrived from various sectors, the source of supply after the exhaustion of the current stock is a major concern. Although parboiled rice has arrived, supplies are scarce. Due to the restraining effect of the shortage of japonica rice, coupled with dull demand, buyers are not very enthusiastic, and prices continue to weaken. Special-grade parboiled rice is priced between 19 yuan 3 and 4 jiao. The market price is only 19 yuan, and the market situation is particularly sluggish. Goods arriving in South Shanghai are still lacking. The market trade is still dominated by foreign rice, but it is reported that several boats may arrive from the south within days. According to news from rice merchants in the interior, the new rice harvests in Jiangxi, Anhui, and Hubei are generally good this year, except for war zones. This new indica rice may be available for shipment downstream in late this month or at the latest in early August. This type of rice is commonly known as early new indica rice. In bumper years, the volume is very large, no less than the japonica rice from Changzhou and Wuxi. Its sales areas are Wuhu, Nanjing, and Wuxi. The goods shipped to Shanghai have already been milled white, so the top-quality rice in this city is this type of rice.

Production volume is limited... High-quality cocoon prices are expected to reach 60 yuan. Although farmers in the four villages of Jiangning raised summer silkworms this year, the cold weather, continuous moldy rain, and subsequent heat caused silkworms to get sick and die during the major molt, resulting in a loss of 70-80%. New summer cocoons have entered the market near the city, and it is estimated that cocoon production will be at most about 30%. The Minfeng Cocoon Company outside Yaohuamen opened yesterday. The initial price of cocoons was 50 yuan. Due to the limited arrival of cocoons, the price rose to 55 yuan. High-quality cocoons are expected to reach 60 yuan.
